Content key: BusinessActivityStartDate

Inline content: The date can't be more than 6 months into the future.

Help content:

ABN start date

The start date should be for when you start setting up your business, not when you start trading.

Actions you might take to start setting up your business include leasing business premises, buying stock or printing business cards.

Content key: BusinessActivityEndDate

Inline content: Businesses registered for GST will be required to complete monthly activity statements.

Help content:

ABN end date

This is the date that you plan to stop all activities for the business.

Please note: If you have also registered for Goods and Services Tax (GST) for a three month period, you'll be required to complete monthly activity statements.

Content key: Password

Inline content: Use at least 8 characters, 1 number, 1 uppercase and 1 lowercase letter.

Help content:

Password

We want your application to be secure, so we ask that you enter a password that meets the following criteria:

  • between 8 and 32 characters
  • at least one number
  • at least one upper case letter
  • at least one lowercase letter.

Forgotten your password?

If you already have a login and you've forgotten your password, click on the Forgotten password? link. This will take you to a page where you can enter a new password.

We will then send you an email to verify the change. Click on the link inside the email to complete the process.

Content key: CompanyNameLegend

Inline content: Do you have a proposed company name?

Help content:

Company name

All companies must choose a company name as part of the company registration process.

If you've reserved your company name already with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC), choose the 'Use a reserved name' option.

What is a company name?

A company name is a company's legal name. This is the name that appears on all official documents and legal papers, such as legal contracts and registrations and property leases.

A company name has two parts:

  • The first part is a name that you choose (we'll check that it's available to register).
  • The second part identifies the company type (such as proprietary limited).
For example: Fishing Supplies Proprietary Limited

If you don't want to choose a name, you can use the company's Australian Company Number (ACN) as the first part of your company name. An ACN is a unique 9 digit number that's issued to your company when it's registered. On company registration certificates and the company register, names that use the ACN will display with 'A.C.N.' at the front.

For example, A.C.N. 123 456 789 Proprietary Limited

Do I also need to register a business name?

If you want to run a business under a name that's different to the company name, you'll need to register that name as a business name.

For example: Jane registers a company with the company name 'Farming Partners Pty Ltd'.

If Jane trades under this exact name (she advertises her company using this name, uses it for her shop signage, etc) then she doesn't need to register a business name.

If she wants to trade under:

  • the name 'Fresh Food', she must register 'Fresh Food' as a business name
  • 'Farming Partners' (without the Pty Ltd), she must register 'Farming Partners' as a business name.

Find out more about registering a business name on the ASIC website.

Content key: CompanyNameUseACN

Help content:

Use ACN

If you don't want to create a name, you can simply use your Australian Company Number (ACN) as the company name.

An ACN is a unique 9 digit number that's issued to your company when it's successfully registered. You still need to include a legal element to identify the company type. On company registration certificates and the company register, names that use the ACN will display with 'A.C.N.' at the front.

For example, A.C.N. 123 456 789 Proprietary Limited.

Content key: DashboardPaymentSuccessful

Inline content: Thank you. Your payment has been received. Your receipt number is @Model.ReceiptNumber.

Please allow up to one business day for the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) to process your application. If you haven't received an update within that time, please contact ASIC online.

Can I get a refund?

If your application is unsuccessful, ASIC will refund your payment. If you don't receive a refund, please contact ASIC online or you can request a refund from ASIC.

Content key: CompanyNameCreateNewNameLabel

Help content:

Company name availability

A company name is not available if it's the same or similar to:

  • another registered company's name
  • a name that's been reserved by another company
  • a registered business name.

If your proposed company name is the same as a registered business name, you can only use it if the owner of the business name is connected to the company in a specific way (e.g. the business name owner is a proposed company member or owner).

There are also certain words or phrases that can only be used if the relevant government agency approves it, such as "university", "building society", etc.

Find out more about choosing company names - see step 2 on ASIC's Starting a company page.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion1

Content key: EntitlementQuestion4

Content key: EntitlementQuestion5

Help content:

Regular or continuous basis

When we say "regular", we mean repeated in a way that follows a general pattern. There?s no set time period for which you must repeat activities. For example, you're selling regularly if you:

  • set up a stall at your local markets every 4 to 6 weeks to sell your products
  • put on exhibitions 3 or 4 times a year to sell your artwork.

When we say "continuous", we mean non-stop. For example, if you earn a continuous income from renting out farming land to one tenant for the next 20 years.

If your business activity isn't ongoing or repeated, or you?re not planning to make a profit or gain, what you?re doing could be more of a hobby than a business. Hobbies don?t need ABNs. For more about this, read the Australian Taxation Office Are you in business? page.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion21

Help content:

Registering a co-operative

To get an ABN for a co-operative, you must first register it with your state or territory authority:

  • NSW Fair Trading
  • VIC ? Consumer Affairs Victoria
  • QLD ? Co-operatives
  • WA Department of Commerce
  • SA Consumer and Business Services
  • TAS Consumer Affairs and Fair Trading
  • ACT ? Co-operatives registration
  • NT ? Co-operatives

Content key: EntitlementQuestion22

Content key: EntitlementQuestion23

Help content:

Incorporating an association

To get an ABN for an incorporated association, you must first register it with your state or territory authority:

  • NSW Fair Trading
  • VIC ? Consumer Affairs Victoria
  • QLD ? Incorporated associations
  • WA Department of Commerce
  • SA - Incorporated associations
  • TAS Consumer Affairs and Fair Trading
  • ACT ? Access Canberra
  • NT ? Incorporated associations

Content key: EntitlementQuestion24

Help content:

Registering foreign companies with ASIC

To be entitled to an ABN, a foreign company must have an Australian Registered Body Number (ARBN).

To get an ARBN, a foreign company must register with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC). Once registered, ASIC will give the company a unique 9 digit ARBN.

Find out more about registering foreign companies with ASIC.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion25

Help content:

Establishment of body corporates

To be entitled to an ABN, a body corporate must either be:

  • established under an Act of Parliament
  • registered under a statute such as the Corporations Act 2001, or
  • incorporated under a state or territory Incorporation Act.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion26

Help content:

Establishment of a corporation sole

To be entitled to an ABN, a corporation sole must be:

  • established under common law
  • established under an Act of Parliament, or
  • registered under a statute.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion27

Content key: EntitlementQuestion28

Help content:

Registering strata titles

To get an ABN for a strata title, you must first register it with your state or territory authority:

  • NSW Land & Property Management Authority ? strata schemes
  • VIC ? Environment, Land, Water & Planning ? owners corporations
  • QLD ? community titles scheme
  • WA Department of Commerce
  • SA Planning, Transport & Infrastructure ? strata titles
  • TAS ? Land Tasmania ? strata title
  • ACT ? Environment & Planning ? unit titles
  • NT ? body corporate

Content key: EntitlementQuestion35

Content key: EntitlementQuestion36

Help content:

Indefinitely continuing fund

An indefinitely continuing fund is a fund that will not terminate or be wound up after a specified period. The intention and expectation is that the fund will continue for the foreseeable future.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion37

Help content:

Sole purpose of the Self-Managed Superannuation Fund (SMSF)

An SMSF must be run for the sole purpose of providing benefits to a member once they reach a prescribed age or upon their retirement, other cessation of employment, or death.

Important: It's illegal to set up an SMSF to gain early access to your super savings. A member?s benefits must be preserved in the fund until they reach their preservation age or until they retire after reaching preservation age.

Visit the ATO's website for details on the SMSF sole purpose test.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion38

Content key: EntitlementQuestion39

Help content:

Governing rules

The governing rules are those contained in a trust deed, other document or legislation ? or a combination of these. Governing rules can also be any unwritten rules governing the establishment or operation of the fund.

Details on what makes up a super fund's governing rules are listed on the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA) website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion107

Content key: EntitlementQuestion108

Help content:

Continuing the enterprise

To be entitled to an Australian Business Number (ABN), the deceased estate must be carrying on the enterprise only for the purpose of finalising the affairs and paperwork of the deceased estate.

For example: Finalising the affairs of a deceased estate with a business can include:
  • selling off assets
  • paying any taxes or debts owed
  • paying any employees owed
  • collecting debts owed to the business
  • cancelling business registrations.

Still not sure?

Trusts are complex business structures, so it's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved. You can also:

  • Check the Deceased estate checklist on the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website.
  • Read more about Deceased estates applying for an ABN on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

Once you?re ready, come back to the Business registration service to complete your registration.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion128

Content key: EntitlementQuestion129

Help content:

Electing to be regulated

A superannuation fund elects to be regulated under the Superannuation Industry (Supervision) Act 1993, in order to receive concessional taxation treatment as a complying super fund.

Important: An election is not valid unless the super fund already has a trust with an appointed trustee.

For details on the licensing and registration of super funds, visit the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA) website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion130

Help content:

Non-Regulated Superannuation Fund

Answer No to this question if you're applying for an ABN for a non-regulated superannuation fund that is not intending to be regulated by the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA) or the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

A non-regulated superannuation fund needs to be exempt under the Superannuation Industry (Supervision) Act 1993(ADD LINK). Examples of non-regulated super funds include:

  • registered financial institutions
  • religious charitable development funds
  • public sector superannuation scheme.

If the trustees intend the super fund to be regulated, they'll need to apply for an APRA-regulated super fund or a self-managed superannuation fund (SMSF).

To read more on non-regulated funds visit APRA's website. You can find more information about regulated super funds at the ATO website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion131

Help content:

Confirmation of intention

The trustee of a unit trust that seeks to be a pooled superannuation trust (PST), or to continue to be treated as a PST, is required to lodge a 'confirmation of intention' form with the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA).

The Trustee should wait for confirmation from APRA, who will send a notice stating that the trust is PST. The PST will then be eligible for concessional tax treatment.

Not sure?

It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you set up a PST.

To find out more about licensing, registration and legal obligations of super funds visit the APRA website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion132

Help content:

Approved purposes

Approved purposes are:

  • receiving on deposit:
    • rollover superannuation benefits
    • directed termination payments
    • amounts paid from roll-overs from eligible rollover funds
    • amounts paid from payments of the shortfall component of a super guarantee charge.
  • dealing with those amounts in accordance with the fund rules
  • repaying deposits and accumulated earnings upon request by the depositor (or by the executor etc. of a deceased depositor)
  • other purposes approved by APRA.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion133

Help content:

Executor of the deceased estate

In order to be entitled to an Australian Business Number (ABN), the deceased estate must have an appointed administrator responsible for the deceased estate.

The administrator can be named in the legal will of the deceased person. This is called the ?executor?.

If a will doesn't exist or the executor for some reason can't complete the role of an administrator, one will be appointed to the deceased estate through a court process.

An executor finalising a deceased estate may carry out activities that meet the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) requirements of 'carrying on a business?, which entitles the deceased estate to an ABN.

Still not sure?

Trusts are complex business structures, so it's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved. You can also:

  • Check the Deceased estate checklist on the ATO website.
  • Read more about Deceased estates applying for an ABN on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

Once you?re ready, come back to the Business registration service to complete your registration.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion134

Help content:

Terms of the trust

The terms of a trust can be set out in a document called a trust deed. A trust deed includes:

  • who the trustee is and their powers and duties in dealing with the trust
  • who the beneficiaries are and their rights
  • what the trust property and assets are and how they are to be dealt with
  • other relevant information.

The terms of a trust can also be implied. This means that the agreement of the parties to a trust is:

  • verbal
  • assumed based on the actions of the parties.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion135

Help content:

GST only registration

You must register for Goods and Services Tax (GST) if you meet the following criteria:

  • you are running a business that is not in Australia
  • your business has sales that are connected with Australia
  • your business has GST turnover at or above A$75,000.

If your business meets the above criteria but your GST turnover is less that A$75,000, you can still choose to register for GST.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion136

Content key: EntitlementQuestion137

Content key: EntitlementQuestion138

Content key: EntitlementQuestion139

Help content:

Started or taking steps to start

If you're just thinking about starting a business, you're not entitled to an ABN.

To be entitled to an ABN, we expect you to have taken several steps to starting a business to show you're committed, such as:

  • meet with financial or business advisers
  • write a business plan
  • estimate your potential business profit
  • apply for finance
  • run feasibility studies
  • lease or buy premises or equipment for the business
  • obtain licences to operate
  • advertise your business.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion143

Help content:

Consistent with running a business

This question is asking whether your activities are consistent with running a business or if they are more like a hobby.

If you're in business and not a hobby:

  • you intend on running a business
  • you plan on making a profit or gain
  • your activities are ongoing or repeated
  • your activities are similar to activities of similar businesses in your industry
  • your activities are carried out in a business-like manner (systematic, organised and records are kept)
  • the size and scale of your activities are reasonable
  • you have a business plan
  • your business has the relevant knowledge or skill.

Your business doesn't need to meet all of the traits listed above, but to be carrying on a business, it's expected that you meet several of them.

For more about this, read the Australian Taxation Office Are you in business? page.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion144

Help content:

Consistent with running a business

This question is asking whether your activities are consistent with running a business or if they are more like a hobby.

If you're in business and not a hobby:

  • you intend on running a business
  • you plan on making a profit or gain
  • your activities are ongoing or repeated
  • your activities are similar to activities of similar businesses in your industry
  • your activities are carried out in a business-like manner (systematic, organised and records are kept)
  • the size and scale of your activities are reasonable
  • you have a business plan
  • your business has the relevant knowledge or skill.

Your business doesn't need to meet all of the traits listed above, but to be carrying on a business, it's expected that you meet several of them.

For more about this, read the Australian Taxation Office Are you in business? page.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion145

Help content:

Consistent with running a business

These questions are to help you work out whether your activities are consistent with running a business or more like a hobby.

If your business activity isn?t ongoing or repeated, or you?re not planning to make a profit or gain, what you?re doing could be more of a hobby than a business. Hobbies don?t need ABNs. For more about this, read the Australian Taxation Office Are you in business? page.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion147

Help content:

Expect to make a profit or gain

This means that you and others have expectations that your activity will make a profit or gain. These expectations are reasonable and not based on risks or luck.

When answering this question consider also that different types of businesses earn profit at different rates.

The definition of 'profit or gain' here is the same as what you would use when talking to your accountant or other businesses.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion151

Help content:

Unincorporated association

Generally, in unincorporated associations:

  • members are free to join or leave as they please
  • members make their own rules on how the group is managed (sometimes called a constitution)
  • there are rules for arranging meetings of members and for appointing officers.

Content key: EntitlementQuestion152

Help content:

Activities carried out in Australia

If you don't run a business in Australia, you may still be entitled to an ABN if you do any of the following.

  • Deliver goods or make goods available in Australia to buyers.
  • Remove goods from Australia.
  • Import, install or assemble goods in Australia.
  • Supply services that are carried out in Australia.
  • Supply property or land that is located in Australia.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer50

Inline content: Body corporates are set up under common law or an Act of Parliament, or registered under a statute.

Help content:

Body corporate

A body corporate is set up by either:

  • establishing it under common law
  • establishing it under an Act of Parliament, or
  • registering it under a statute.

A body corporate is a legal entity that is separate from its individual members. It can act, hold property, enter into legal contracts, sue and be sued in its own name.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer51

Inline content: A corporation that consists of a particular position, such as a bishop in a church.

Help content:

Corporation sole

A corporation sole is set up by either:

  • establishing it under common law
  • establishing it under an Act of Parliament, or
  • registering it under a statute.

A corporation sole is a corporation that consists of a particular position, such as:

  • an archbishop
  • a bishop in a church
  • a minister of the Crown.

A corporation sole is separate from the individual who occupies the position. The position is a legal entity, no matter who holds the position, and even if the position is vacant from time to time.

In the name of the position, a corporation sole can own property, sue and be sued.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer52

Inline content: Companies set up outside Australia or in an external territory of Australia (such as Christmas Island).

Help content:

Foreign company

A foreign company is a company that was set up:

  • outside Australia or
  • in an external territory of Australia, such as Christmas Island or Norfolk Island.

To carry on business in Australia, foreign companies must register with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC). Once registered, they will get a unique 9 digit Australian Registered Body Number (ARBN).

Find out more about registering foreign companies with ASIC.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer53

Inline content: Organisations like clubs or community groups that are incorporated under state or territory law.

Help content:

Incorporated association

Incorporated associations are usually clubs or community groups that have decided to give their organisation a formal legal structure.

Incorporated associations usually have at least five members. They must use all profits to achieve the association's aims.

When a club or group incorporates, it becomes a separate legal entity (separate from its members). It can do things in its own name, such as lease a property or be sued. This protects the members from any legal liability.

Associations are incorporated under state or territory legislation. They can only operate in that state or territory.

To operate outside its state or territory of incorporation, an incorporated association must register with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) under the Corporations Act 2001.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer338

Inline content: Including apprentices, trade assistants and labourers.

Help content:

Apprentice, trade assistant or labourer

You don?t need an ABN to work as an apprentice, trade assistant, or labourer. You work under the direction of your employer, so you?re actually an employee.

If your employer is asking you to register as a contractor when you?re really an employee, you can report the business to the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

If you're not sure whether you're an employee or not, try our independent contractors decision tool.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer339

Inline content: Activities that are business-like in nature.

Help content:

In the form of a business

This means activities that are business-like in nature, including selling products or services to make a profit. Your activities are also in the form of a business if you're:

  • an independent contractor
  • a taxi or limousine travel service operator
  • a club or society
  • a non-profit organisation
  • a body corporate.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer340

Inline content: Such as an apartment or house.

Help content:

Renting or leasing out a residential property

If you rent or lease out a residential property, you're entitled to an Australian Business Number (ABN) if you:

  • rent out the property on a regular or continuous basis
  • intend on making a profit.

Please note: If you rent out property to be used mainly for residential accommodation purposes, you don't need an ABN.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer341

Inline content: Such as land, cars, copyright or patents.

Help content:

In the form of a licence, lease or other grant of an interest in property

This is when you have property (such as land, cars, boats, copyright or patents) and you offer a licence, lease or other type of interest in that property to someone else.

You're entitled to an ABN for this activity if you:

  • offer this on a regular or continuous basis
  • intend on making a profit.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer344

Inline content: Business-like deals or sales that aren't part of an on-going business.

Help content:

One-off commercial transactions not done in the course of a business

These are financial transactions or business-like deals that are not done as part of an on-going business for example the sale of property.

These transactions are one-off and have a reasonable expectation of profit or gain.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer349

Help content:

Deductible Gift Recipient (DGR)

A DGR is a not-for-profit organisation endorsed by the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

A DGR is entitled to receive income tax deductible gifts and tax deductible contributions.

Please note: A DGR does not automatically receive tax concessions. This requires a separate endorsement by the ATO.

There are two types of DGR endorsement:

  • where an entity is endorsed as a whole, for example, public hospitals or public universities
  • where an entity is endorsed for the operation of a fund, authority or institution that it owns or includes, for example, school building funds or council libraries.

For the second type, only gifts to the fund, authority or institution are tax deductible.

Not all DGR's are registered charities that are exempt from income tax. Find out why on fundraising and income taxpage.

For more information on not-for-profits, visit the non-profit page on the ATO website.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer350

Help content:

Charity

A charity is a not-for-profit organisation registered with the Australian Charities and Not-for-profits Commission (ACNC).

Charities can receive tax concessions for income, fringe benefits tax and goods and services tax. To receive these tax concessions, a charity must first be endorsed by the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

A charity can also be a Deductible Gift Recipient (DGR), but not all charities are DGRs. The two require separate endorsement from the ATO.

For more information visit the non-profit page on the ATO website.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer354

Inline content: Business-like deals or sales that aren't part of an on-going business.

Help content:

One-off commercial transactions not done in the course of a business

These are financial transactions or business-like deals that are not done as part of an on-going business for example the sale of property. These transactions are one-off and have a reasonable expectation of profit or gain.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer355

Help content:

Deductible Gift Recipient (DGR)

A DGR is a not-for-profit organisation endorsed by the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

A DGR is entitled to receive income tax deductible gifts and tax deductible contributions.

Please note: A DGR does not automatically receive tax concessions. This requires a separate endorsement by the ATO.

There are two types of DGR endorsement:

  • where an entity is endorsed as a whole, for example, public hospitals or public universities
  • where an entity is endorsed for the operation of a fund, authority or institution that it owns or includes, for example, school building funds or council libraries.

For the second type, only gifts to the fund, authority or institution are tax deductible.

Not all DGR's are registered charities that are exempt from income tax. Find out why on fundraising and income taxpage.

For more information on not-for-profits, visit the non-profit page on the ATO website.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer356

Help content:

Charity

A charity is a not-for-profit organisation registered with the Australian Charities and Not-for-profits Commission (ACNC).

Charities can receive tax concessions for income, fringe benefits tax and goods and services tax. To receive these tax concessions, a charity must first be endorsed by the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

A charity can also be a Deductible Gift Recipient (DGR), but not all charities are DGRs. The two require separate endorsement from the ATO.

For more information visit the non-profit page on the ATO website.

You can also read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer357

Inline content: Activities that are business-like in nature.

Help content:

In the form of a business

This means activities that are business-like in nature, including selling products or services to make a profit. Your activities are also in the form of a business if you're:

  • an independent contractor
  • a taxi or limousine travel service operator
  • a club or society
  • a non-profit organisation
  • a body corporate.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer358

Help content:

Renting or leasing out a residential property

Not all individuals that rent or lease out a residential property need an ABN. However, if these activities are performed on a regular or continuous basis with the intention of making a profit, you're entitled to an ABN.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAnswer359

Inline content: Such as land, cars, copyright or patents.

Help content:

In the form of a licence, lease or other grant of an interest in property

This is when you have property (such as land, cars, boats, copyright or patents) and you offer a licence, lease or other type of interest in that property to someone else. You're entitled to an ABN for this activity if you offer this on a regular or continuous basis with the intention of making a profit.

You can read more about ABN entitlement on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: CompanyNameCreateNewNameLabel

Help content:

Company name availability

A company name is not available if it's the same or similar to:

  • another registered company's name
  • a name that's been reserved by another company
  • a registered business name.

If your proposed company name is the same as a registered business name, you can only use it if the owner of the business name is connected to the company in a specific way (e.g. the business name owner is a proposed company member or owner).

There are also certain words or phrases that can only be used if the relevant government agency approves it, such as "university", "building society", etc.

Find out more about choosing company names - see step 2 on ASIC's Starting a company page.

Content key: BusinessAssociateRuleAPUB

Did you know? Individuals can hold more than one role. For example, you can be both a director, a secretary and a shareholder.

Content key: CompanyGovern

Help content:

Will the company be governed by a constitution?

A public company must have rules for how it will be governed or managed. For example, rules for how directors will be appointed and how shareholder meetings will be organised.

Most companies can be governed by a constitution, replaceable rules, or a combination of both.

Replaceable rules

Replaceable rules are a basic set of rules for managing a company. They are set out in the Corporations Act 2001.

Using replaceable rules means you don?t need to worry about having or maintaining your own written constitution (or dealing with the expense of keeping the constitution up to date with the law).

These rules are called 'replaceable' rules because you can replace all or some of the rules with a constitution.

Read an outline of the replaceable rules on the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) website.

Constitution

A company can use its own constitution instead of the replaceable rules, or use a constitution to replace some of the replaceable rules.

If the company has more than one shareholder (member), they must all agree to the terms and conditions of a constitution before the company can adopt it.

If your company will be governed by a constitution (either fully or partly), you'll need to upload a copy in the next step of the form.

Find out more

Find out more about constitutions and replaceable rules on the ASIC website.

Name available

Even if your name meets the business naming rules, the same name could still be registered by someone else as a trade mark or domain name. If you want exclusive use of your business name take the following steps to protect it:

Content key: BusinessDetailsContactResidentialAddressLegend

Inline content: Residential address

Help content:

Residential address

Your residential address is where you live, not necessarily where you run your business. We ask this to check your identity.

Please note: Your residential address can't be a post office box.

If you don't have a separate business address, your residential address will also be listed as your main business address.

Your privacy

If your residential address and main business address are the same, the public register will only display your suburb, postcode and state or territory.

Find out more about how the following agencies will use and protect your information:

  • Australian Business Register (ABR)
  • Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC).

Content key: BusinessDetailsContactBusinessAddressLegend

Inline content: Main business address

Help content:

Main business address

Your main business address is where you operate your main business activity.

Please note: Under business name registration, the main business address is known as the "Principal place of business".

If you have multiple business locations, enter your head office here.

For home businesses, enter your residential address. If your home address and main business address are the same, the public register will only display your suburb, postcode and state or territory.

Please note: This must be a physical address in Australia. Postal addresses will not be accepted.

If there is no physical place of business, enter the street address for the place where your business records are kept.

Content key: BusinessDetailsContactPostalAddressLegend

Help content:

Postal address

We collect a postal address so that the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) and the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) can send notices and correspondence to your business.

Business name registration

Under business name registration, the postal address is known as the "Address for service of documents".

Please note: If you've applied for a business name, this postal address will appear on the public Business Names Register.

If your postal address and residential address are the same, and making it public poses a risk - you can submit a request to suppress the address from the ASIC Business names register.

Content key: BusinessDetailsContactAuthorisedContactLegend

Inline content: Authorised contact

Help content:

Authorised contact

You can choose to nominate one or more people to be authorised contacts for your business name, ABN and tax registrations.

For ABN or tax registration, an authorised contact can ask the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) to change your details on your behalf. Find out more about ATO authorised contacts on the ATO website.

For business name registration, an authorised contact can complete transactions with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) on your behalf. Find out more about Authorised lodgers for business names on the ASIC website.

An authorised contact can't add, remove or update your authorised contacts unless they declare they've been given authority to do so by you.

You can nominate any individual to become your authorised contact, as long as they meet POI (Proof of Identity) requirements. Authorised contacts can include:

  • registered tax agents
  • registered BAS agents
  • lawyers
  • guardians
  • family members or friends.

Content key: EntitlementAbnDetailsBusinessChristmasCocosIsland

Help content:

Christmas Island or Cocos Island

You can register a business name without an ABN if you operate solely on Christmas Island or Cocos (Keeling) Island.

You'll need to tell us whether you're:

  • an individual (sole trader)
  • an organisation with an Australian Company Number (ACN) or Australian Registered Body Number (ARBN)
  • an organisation with no ACN or ARBN (this includes partnerships and joint ventures).
ACNs and ARBNs are unique 9 digit numbers issued to companies and other organisations registered with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC).

Content key: EntitlementAbnDetailsRegisteringJointVenture

Inline content: A joint venture is usually formed for a specific project or goal with an end date (unlike a partnership, which is usually ongoing).

Help content:

Joint venture (all partners have an ABN)

Joint ventures without an ABN can apply for a business name if all partners in the joint venture have:

  • their own ABN, or
  • an ABN application reference number.

You'll need to provide the following information about the joint venture partners:

  • Individuals ? their name, birth details and residential address
  • Companies or registered bodies ? their Australian Company Number (ACN) or Australian Registered Body Number (ARBN)
  • Organisations without an ACN or ARBN (including partnerships) ? their ABN and name, and details of a representative for that partner (the representative can be an individual or an incorporated entity).

Place of birth

Please only enter the city or town of birth and check it:

Content key: CompanyAssociates

Help content:

Business associates

In this section, please provide the details of all business associates of the company, including:

  • directors
  • shareholders or members
  • secretaries.

Companies must have written consent from all directors, secretaries and shareholders/members to take on their role. You don't need to provide copies, but you must keep them as part of the company's records after the company is registered.

As the applicant, you'll be asked to declare that you have received these before you can submit this application.

Remember! Shareholders/members can be individuals or companies, but directors and secretaries must be individuals.

What personal information will be available to the public?

The following information will be available to the public in the company register:

  • All directors and secretaries ? their full name, date of birth and residential address.
  • Top 20 shareholders or members (based on shareholdings) of each share class ? their name and address.

Officeholders (directors and secretaries) can apply for approval to provide a different address in some circumstances. Visit the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) website for information about the application fee and how to apply for suppression of residential address.

Read the summary of ASIC's privacy policy to find out how ASIC handles personal information.

Content key: CompanyRegOfficeNote

Inline content: This is where we will send official documents and notices. Must be a street address. Does not have to be the same as the main place of business.

Help content:

Registered office

All companies must provide a registered office address. This is where ASIC will send certain official documents and notices.

A registered office must be a street address in Australia (not a post office box).

If the company doesn't occupy the address, the company must get written consent from the occupier.

Find out more about company addresses on the ASIC website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsLegendNote

Content key: SelectRegistrationsABN

Help content:

Australian Business Number (ABN)

An ABN is a unique 11 digit number that identifies your business to the public, the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) and other government agencies.

Applying for an ABN is free, but not everyone is entitled to one.

Why should I have an ABN?

If you're running a business, you may need an ABN. Having an ABN means you can:

  • confirm your business identity to others when ordering and invoicing
  • avoid having business clients withhold a percentage of any payments they make to you
  • register a business name
  • register a '.com.au', '.net.au', or '.org.au' domain name.

You also need to have an ABN if you register for Goods and Services Tax (GST)

You don't need an ABN if the business is:

  • located in the Christmas or Cocos Islands
  • a joint venture (where the partners have their own ABNs).

Do I also need a business TFN?

If you're applying for an ABN for a partnership, company or trust, you'll need a business TFN.

The good news is you don't need to register. The ATO will automatically issue the partnership, company or trust with a TFN (if one doesn't already exist).

Can I use my old ABN?

You can reuse a previous ABN if the old business had the same entity type as the new one.

Please note: If the entity types are different, you?ll be issued with a new ABN.

To reuse a previous ABN, first apply for a new ABN here on the Business registration service. Once this application is successful, the Australian Business Registrar can then issue you with your old ABN.

Find out more

See the Australian Business Register's ABN Explained page for more details.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsBusinessName

Inline content: $35+

Help content:

Business name

A business name, also known as a trading name, is a name or title under which a person, or other legal entity, carries on business. It also helps customers and other businesses find, identify and connect with your business.

You need to register a business name if you conduct business under a name other than your own.

Discover more about business names and when to register one on the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) website.

Registering a business name

When you register a business name, you register it nationally with ASIC. This means you can operate your business in any state or territory in Australia.

See the things you need to consider before registering a business name on the ASIC website.

Protecting your business name

Registering a business name doesn't stop others from using it! Before you register a business name, consider these steps:

  • Check existing names: Search ASIC's Registers to see if the business name is available.
  • Check existing trade marks: Make sure you?re not infringing on someone else?s intellectual property (IP). Visit the IP Australia website to find out about searching for trade marks in Australia and overseas.
  • Register a web address: If you want to use your proposed business name as part of your web address, see our information on registering a domain name.
  • Apply for a trade mark: To protect your business name, apply for a trade mark on the IP Australia website.

Find out the difference between a business name, trade mark, company name and domain name on the ASIC website.

Visit the IP Australia website for details on how to protect your name and other brands.

Renewing your business name

You need to renew your business name regularly. You can pay yearly or every three years. See the business name renewal fees on the ASIC website.

The Business registration service does not currently process business name renewals. See the different options available for renewing your business name on the ASIC website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsPAYGw

Help content:

Pay As You Go (PAYG) withholding

You must be registered for PAYG withholding before you need to withhold tax amounts from payments such as:

  • the wage or salary payments you make to employees
  • payments to directors
  • payments to businesses that do not quote their ABN to you
  • royalty, dividend or interest payments to non-residents
  • investment income payments to Australian residents (if you're an investment body).

You must then forward these tax amounts to the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

PAYG withholding isn't a tax on your business - it's a tax on your employees' income that you help the ATO to collect.

Check to see if you need to register for PAYG withholding on the ATO website.

What do I need to do?

Being registered for PAYG withholding means you:

  • work out how much you need to withhold
  • report PAYG withholding amounts to the ATO
  • pay PAYG withholding amounts to the ATO when they're due
  • include PAYG withholding amounts in your employees' pay slips and payment summaries.

Find out more

See how PAYG withholding works on the ATO website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsTFN

Help content:

Business Tax File Number (TFN)

All partnerships, companies and trusts need a business TFN to deal with the Australian Taxation Office, for example to report business income and deductions.

The good news is you don't need to register. The ATO will automatically issue a partnership, company or trust with a TFN (if one doesn't already exist).

Sole traders can use their personal TFN for both their personal and business matters. Find out more about TFNs for business on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsFBT

Help content:

Fringe Benefits Tax (FBT)

As an employer, if you give certain fringe benefits to your employees, you must pay tax on the value of the fringe benefits.

You'll need to register for FBT before you start providing these benefits.

Visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website to:

  • find out what types of fringe benefits you must pay tax on
  • check if you need to register for FBT.

What do I need to do?

Being registered for FBT means you:

  • work out how much FBT you have to pay
  • keep records related to the fringe benefits you provide
  • report fringe benefits on your employees' payment summaries
  • report fringe benefits to the ATO
  • pay the FBT to the ATO.

Find out more

Read about FBT for small business on the ATO website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsLCT

Help content:

Luxury Car Tax (LCT)

LCT is a tax on the supply and import of cars that exceed the LCT threshold.

You must register for LCT if you sell or import luxury cars.

To register for LCT you must also be registered for Goods and Services Tax (GST).

Visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website to:

  • check if you need to register for LCT
  • find out this year's LCT threshold.

What do I need to do?

Being registered for LCT means you:

  • work out the LCT payable and include it in the import or sale
  • account for LCT sales and imports in your books
  • report and pay LCT to the ATO.

Find out more

Go to the ATO website for more about:

  • working out the LCT amount you need to pay
  • Luxury Car Tax.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsFTC

Help content:

Fuel Tax Credits (FTC)

If you register for FTC, you can claim credits for the fuel tax you pay on eligible fuels. The amount of FTC you can claim depends on the type of fuel you use and the business activity you use it in.

To be eligible, you must:

  • be registered for GST
  • use eligible fuels in eligible business activities.

Visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website to:

  • view eligible liquid and gaseous fuels
  • view eligible business activities
  • use the FTC eligibility tool

What do I need to do?

Being registered for FTC means you:

  • work out how much you can claim on eligible fuels
  • keep records of the type and quantity of fuels, when you bought the fuels and how you used them in your business.

Find out more

Read more about Fuel Tax Credits on the ATO website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsWET

Help content:

Wine Equalisation Tax (WET)

You must register for WET and GST if you produce or sell wholesale wines that WET applies to.

WET applies to grape wines, fruit wines, vegetable wines, cider, perry, mead, and sake (where they contain more than 1.15% by volume of ethyl alcohol).

Visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website to:

  • find out more about the products WET applies to
  • check if you need to register for WET.

What is WET?

WET is a tax on the consumption of wine in Australia, and it's usually applied to the last wholesale sale - this is usually the sale to the retailer. You collect the tax to give to the ATO.

What do I need to do?

Being registered for WET means you:

  • work out which sales are subject to WET
  • calculate the WET amount
  • issue tax invoices that show the WET amount
  • claim any WET credits you may be entitled to (including rebates or refunds)
  • account for WET amounts in your books
  • put aside WET you've collected
  • report and pay WET to the ATO.

Find out more

Read more about Wine Equalisation Tax on the ATO website.

Content key: EntitlementAbnIntroText

Inline content: Before you continue, we need to first check that you?re entitled to an ABN.

Content key: EntitlementAbnEntityTypeIntro

Inline content: Select the business structure that best describes the business. If you need help deciding on a business structure, see our Business structure decision tool

Content key: EntitlementAbnEntityTypeSoleTrader

Help content:

Individual (Sole trader)

If you're a sole trader, you're the sole owner of the business. The income your business makes belongs to you. You report the income in your personal tax return and pay tax on your business income at your individual tax rate.

You're responsible for all decisions and losses in your business. This means you have complete control over your business, but it also means your personal assets are at risk if things go wrong.

If you employ staff, you're responsible for giving them their minimum employee entitlements and conditions (such as superannuation and leave).

Content key: EntitlementAbnEntityTypePartnership

Help content:

Partnership

In a partnership structure, you and your business partners own the business together and share the income and losses of the business. A partnership can have two to twenty partners. You're in a family partnership structure if two or more of the partners are related.

Each partner reports their share of the income in their own personal tax return. An annual partnership return must also be lodged with the Australian Taxation Office.

All partners share legally responsibility for the business. This means the personal assets of all partners are at risk if things go wrong. If some partners want to limit their responsibility for business losses, you might want to consider a limited partnership structure.

If your business employs staff, all partners are responsible for giving staff their minimum employee entitlements and conditions (such as superannuation and leave).

Content key: EntitlementAbnEntityTypeCompany

Help content:

Company

A company structure means that your business is a separate legal entity from you. This means the company has the same rights as a natural person and can have debt, sue and be sued.

A company must have at least:

  • one owner (known as a shareholder or member), and
  • one director (who is responsible for running the business, and for business debts in some cases).

You can be both. You can also set up a one person company and not have any other owner or director.

Shareholders are generally not responsible for any losses, so your personal assets are generally not at risk if things go wrong.

The income and losses that the business makes belongs to the company, and is reported in a company tax return.

If the company employs staff, the company is responsible for giving them their minimum employee entitlements and conditions (such as superannuation and leave).

Content key: EntitlementAbnEntityTypeTrust

Help content:

Trust

Using a trust structure for your business means that your business is held and controlled by a trustee for the benefit of others (the beneficiaries). A trustee is responsible for everything in the trust, including income and losses, and must report income in a trust income tax return. A trustee can be a company or a person.

Content key: EntitlementAbnEntityTypeSuperannuation

Help content:

Superannuation

This means all superannuation entities including Self-Managed Super Funds (SMSFs).

Content key: EntitlementAbnActivitiesAustralia

Help content:

Activities carried out in Australia

If you do not operate in Australia, you may still be entitled to an ABN if you do any of the following:
  • Deliver goods or make goods available in Australia to buyers.
  • Remove goods from Australia.
  • Import, install or assemble goods in Australia.
  • Supply property or land that is located in Australia.
  • Supply services that are carried out in Australia.

Content key: EntitlementAbnIndirectTaxZone

Inline content: Indirect tax zone means Australia, excluding external territories or offshore areas such as Christmas Island, Cocos Island, and the Joint Petroleum Area.

Help content:

Supplies connected with the indirect tax zone

Indirect tax zone means Australia, excluding external territories or offshore areas such as Christmas Island, Cocos Island and the Joint Petroleum Area.

If you do not operate in Australia, you may still be entitled to an ABN if you do any of the following:

  • Deliver goods or make goods available in Australia to buyers
  • Remove goods from Australia
  • Import, install or assemble goods in Australia.
  • Supply services that are carried out in Australia
  • Supply property or land that is located in Australia.

Content key: EntitlementAbnGstOnly

Help content:

GST only registration

You must register for Goods and Services Tax (GST) if you meet the following criteria:

  • you are running a business that is not in Australia
  • still waiting on response on this - your business has sales that are connected with Australia
  • your business has GST turnover at or above A$75,000.

If your business meets the above criteria but your GST turnover is less than A$75,000, you can still choose to register for GST.

Content key: EntitlementAbnTakingSteps

Help content:

Started or taking steps to start

If you're just thinking about starting a business, you're not eligible for an ABN.

To be eligible for an ABN, we expect you to have taken several steps to starting a business to show you're committed, such as:

  • meet with financial or business advisers
  • write a business plan
  • estimate your potential business profit
  • apply for finance
  • run feasibility studies
  • lease or buy premises or equipment for the business
  • obtain licences to operate
  • advertise your business.

Content key: EntitlementAbnNatureActivityApprentice

Help content:

Apprentice, trade assistant or labourer

You don?t need an ABN to work as an apprentice, trade assistant, or labourer. You work under the direction of your employer, so you?re actually an employee.

If your employer is asking you to register as a contractor when you?re really an employee, you can report the business to the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

If you?re not sure whether you?re an employee or not, try the ATO?s Employee/contractor decision tool.

Content key: EntitlementAbnNatureActivityInFormOfBusiness

Inline content: Activities that are business-like in nature.

Help content:

In the form of a business

This means activities that are business-like in nature including selling products or services to make a profit. Your activities are also in the form of a business if you're:
  • an independent contractor
  • a taxi or limousine travel service operator
  • a club or society
  • a non-profit organisation
  • a body corporate.

Content key: EntitlementAbnNatureActivityRentLease

Help content:

Renting or leasing out a residential property

Not all individuals that rent or lease out a residential property need an ABN. However, if these activities are performed on a regular or continuous basis with the intention of making a profit, you're entitled to an ABN.

Content key: EntitlementAbnNatureActivityLicenceLease

Inline content: Such as land, cars, copyright or patents.

Help content:

In the form of a licence, lease or other grant of an interest in property

This is when you have property (such as land, cars, boats, copyright or patents) and you offer a licence, lease or other type of interest in that property to someone else. You're entitled to an ABN for this activity if you offer this on a regular or continuous basis with the intention of making a profit.

Content key: EntitlementAbnNatureActivityOneOffCommercial

Inline content: Business-like deals or sales that aren't part of an on-going business..

Help content:

One-off commercial transactions not done in the course of a business

These are financial transactions or business-like deals that are not done as part of an on-going business for example the sale of property. These transactions are one-off and have a reasonable expectation of profit or gain.

Content key: EntitlementAbnConsistentRunningBusiness

Help content:

Consistent with running a business

These questions are to help you work out whether your activities are consistent with running a business or more like a hobby.

If your business activity isn?t ongoing or repeated, or you?re not planning to make a profit or gain, what you?re doing could be more of a hobby than a business. Hobbies don?t need ABNs. For more about this, read the Australian Taxation Office Are you in business? page.

You can also read more about ABN eligibility on the Australian Business Register website.

Content key: EntitlementAbnRegularContinuousBasis

Help content:

Regular or continuous basis

When we say ?regularly?, we mean repeatedly in a way that follows a general pattern. There?s no set time period for which you must repeat activities. For example, you?re selling regularly if you:

  • set up a stall at your local markets every 4 to 6 weeks to sell your products
  • put on exhibitions 3 or 4 times a year to sell your artwork.

When we say ?continuously?, we mean non-stop. For example, if you earn a continuous income from renting out farming land to one tenant for the next 20 years.

If your business activity isn?t ongoing or repeated, or you?re not planning to make a profit or gain, what you?re doing could be more of a hobby than a business. Hobbies don?t need ABNs. For more about this, read the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) Are you in business? page.

Content key: EntitlementAbnExpectProfitGain

Help content:

Expect to make a profit or gain

This means that you and others have expectations that your activity will make a profit or gain. These expectations are reasonable and not based on risks or luck.

Content key: BusinessNameTransferKey

Inline content: Please enter your transfer number.

Help content:

Transfer number

Please enter a transfer number that is:

  • no more than 23 characters
  • in the format n-nnnnnnnnnnn or nn-nnnnnnnnnnn.

If you've bought a business and want to use the existing business name, you'll need the transfer number from the previous owner before you can register it.

If you haven't received a transfer number from the previous owner, you'll need to contact them.

More information

Find out more about transferring business names.

Content key: BusinessActivityDetailsTAN

Help content:

Tax agent registration number

The tax agent number (TAN) is an 8 digit number given to tax agents when they are registered.

You can find this number on an income tax return prepared by your tax agent.

If the TAN number you find is only 7 digits, add a '0' at the beginning of your number to complete this field.

Content key: BusinessDetailsPoiTfnIntro

Inline content: Providing your TFN is the quickest way to prove your identity.

Help content:

Tax File Number (TFN)

Do I have to provide my TFN?

No you don't have to provide your TFN. However, not providing one will delay your application. It may also lead to an unsuccessful application if your identity can't be confirmed without a TFN.

TFN is mandatory if you apply for an AUSkey at the same time as your ABN.

Why the delay?

Without a TFN, the Australian Business Register (ABR) may need to manually process your application. To do this, the ABR will need you to provide additional information or certified copies of documents including your:

  • bank account number
  • birth certificate
  • passport
  • driver?s licence.

Can I provide my TFN later?

If you don't have your TFN with you, you can leave the form and come back to it later. The form will be saved automatically.

As long as you don't lodge the form, you can return later and log in to resume your application from the Application summary screen.

Where can I find out more?

Details on what information the ABR needs to prove your identity can be found on the ABR website.

Content key: BusinessDetailsWhyAbnFirstTime

Help content:

First time in business

Answer Yes to this question if you've never owned or operated a business in Australia. This includes as a sole trader, partner, trustee, director or contractor/subcontractor.

Content key: TaxDetailsGstStartDate

Help content:

GST start date

If you're required by law to register for GST, your GST registration should start on the date:

  • your annual turnover reached $75,000 or more
  • you started charging passengers for taxi services or limousine travel (including ride-sharing)
  • you want to start claiming fuel tax credits.

If you choose to register for GST, you can choose any start date, as long as it's the same as or later than your ABN start date.

Important: You?re expected to stay registered for at least 12 months. If you apply for your GST registration to be cancelled within 12 months, you may be refused or be required to report monthly.

Visit the ATO website to find out more about GST.

Content key: TaxDetailsGstTurnover

Help content:

GST turnover

GST turnover is your current or projected annual turnover (excluding GST amounts) - whichever is greater. GST turnover is not your profit.

Current annual turnover is:

  • the value of all sales you made or are likely to make in the current month plus
  • the value of all sales you made in the previous 11 months.

Projected annual turnover is:

  • the value of all sales you made or are likely to make in the current month plus
  • the value of all sales you're likely to make in the next 11 months.

If you need more help working out your annual GST turnover visit the ATO website.

Content key: SelectRegistrationsDescription

Inline content: Welcome to the Australian Government Business Registration Service.
Here you can apply for your key business and tax registrations in one place.

Are you new to business? To help you get started, see business.gov.au's Starting your business checklist and download a business plan template.

Help content:

Select registrations

Welcome to the Australian Government Business Registration Service Public Beta. The service combines a number of key government business and tax registration forms in one place including:

  • Australian Business Number (ABN)
  • Business name
  • Goods and Services Tax (GST)*
  • Australian company
  • Pay as You Go (PAYG) withholding*
  • Fringe Benefits Tax (FBT)*
  • Luxury Car Tax (LCT)*
  • Fuel Tax Credits (FTC)*
  • Wine Equalisation Tax (WET)*
  • Administrator AUSkey*.

*At the moment on the New business section of the Business registration service, you can only apply for the registrations indicated above together with a business or company application.

If you already have an ABN and want to apply for:

  • a tax registration, please visit the Apply for tax registrations page.
  • an AUSkey login, please visit the Apply for AUSkey login page.

What is a Public Beta website?

A public beta website is typically a real working website or service in its final testing stage. A beta is used to receive public feedback to help improve the service.

Please note: Even though the Business Registration Service is in beta, the registrations you apply for are real!

So if you use the Business Registration Service, please give us your feedback.

What does it cost to register?

There is no charge to register for tax registrations, but there is a fee for the following:

  • Business name - For each business name, you can pay $35 for 1 year or $82 for 3 years. See the current list of business name fees on the ASIC website.
  • Australian company - The cost depends on the type of company you register. For example you'll pay $479 to register a proprietary limited company. See the current list of company fees on the ASIC website.

Where can I register for a business TFN?

If you're applying for an ABN for a partnership, company or trust you'll need a business TFN.

The good news is you don't need to register. The ATO will automatically issue a partnership, company or trust with a TFN (if one doesn't already exist).

Can I register Norfolk Island businesses here?

Yes. Norfolk Island businesses can apply here for the following business registrations:

  • Australian Business Number (ABN)
  • Business name
  • Australian company ? if operating on the Australian mainland
  • Pay As You Go (PAYG) withholding
  • Fringe Benefits Tax (FBT)
  • AUSKey

Norfolk Island businesses do not need to register for Goods and Services Tax (GST), Luxury Car Tax (LCT), Fuel Tax Credits (FTC) or Wine Equalisation Tax (WET).

Norfolk Island companies are registered with the Norfolk Island Registry.

However, if your Norfolk Island company is or will be operating on the Australian mainland, you'll need to register as a foreign company with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC).

Find out about registering foreign companies on the ASIC website.

Can I update my details or apply for renewals here?

Not at the moment. The Business registration form only accepts new business or tax registrations.

To update or renew your registrations you'll need to refer to the correspondence you receive confirming your registration.

If you can't find your correspondence, visit the following agency websites to:

  • update your company details or annual statements on the ASIC website
  • update or renew your business name on the ASIC website
  • update your tax details for your ABN, GST, PAYG, TFN, FBT, LCT, FTC, WET registrations on the ATO website.

Can I apply here for state licences or permits?

No. You'll still need to find and apply for your business licences and permits on the Australian Business Licence & Information Service (ABLIS) website.

Where do I go for help?

If you have a question about the form or how your registrations are progressing, contact business.gov.au on 13 28 46

Content key: EntitlementEntityTypeLegend

Inline content: Select a business structure that best describes the business. If you need help deciding on a business structure, see our Help me decide tool.

Content key: EntitlementEntityTypeIND

Inline content: An individual or a sole trader is where you're the sole owner of the business, but you can employ staff. You're responsible for all decisions and losses in your business, and you report the business income in your personal tax return.

Help content:

Individual (Sole trader)

If you're a sole trader, you're an individual and the sole owner of the business. The income your business makes belongs to you. You report the income in your personal tax return and pay tax on your business income at your individual tax rate.

You're responsible for all decisions and losses in your business. This means you have complete control over your business, but it also means your personal assets are at risk if things go wrong.

If you employ staff, you're responsible for giving them their minimum employee entitlements and conditions (such as superannuation and leave).

Content key: EntitlementEntityTypePTR

Inline content: You and your partners carry on a business together and share income, losses and control of the business. The partnership can employ staff, but the partners in the partnership are not considered employees.

Help content:

Partnership

A partnership is a group of people in business together and who may have a written partnership agreement.

In a partnership structure, you and your partners own the business together and share the income and losses of the business. A partnership can have two or more partners. You're in a family partnership structure if two or more of the partners are related.

The partnership needs its own TFN and will have to lodge an annual partnership return with the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) showing all income and deductions of the business and the distributions to each partner. Also, each partner reports their share of the income or loss in their own personal tax return. Each partner will pay tax on the share of profits they receive.

Select Partnership on this form if your partnership is one of the following:

  • Family partnership: where two or more partners are related.
  • Other partnership: where two or more partners form a general partnership.
Looking for Limited partnerships? Please select the company structure to find the limited partnership type.

Find out more

More on the partnership business structure can be found on the business.gov.au website.

To find out more about the different types of partnership visit the Australian Business Register website.

To find out if you're a partnership for tax purposes, visit the Australian Taxation Office website.

Content key: EntitlementEntityTypeCOY

Inline content: A company is a separate legal entity from you, and has at least one shareholder or member and one director (who runs the business). Income and losses belong to the company. Companies can employ staff.

Help content:

Company

A company structure means that your business is a separate legal entity from you. This means the company has the same rights as a natural person and can have debt, sue and be sued.

Companies have minimum shareholder/member and officeholder requirements. For example, a proprietary limited company (the most common company type in Australia) must have at least:

  • one shareholder
  • one director (who is responsible for running the business, and for business debts in some cases).

The income and losses that the business makes belongs to the company, and is reported in a company tax return.

If the company employs staff, the company is responsible for giving them their minimum employee entitlements and conditions (such as superannuation and leave).

Content key: EntitlementEntityTypeTRT

Inline content: Your business or businesslike activity is held and controlled for the benefit of others (the beneficiaries). A trustee is responsible for everything in the trust, including income and losses.

Help content:

Trust

To be considered a trust for tax purposes, the entity must have:

  • a business or businesslike activity (such as charitable, leasing or one-off transactions) held and controlled for the benefit of others (the beneficiaries).
  • a trustee responsible for everything in the trust, including income and losses. The trustee can be a person or an incorporated company.
  • an object or purpose of the trust implied or in writing, often in the form of a trust deed.

Important: Applying for an Australian Business Number (ABN) doesn't automatically form a trust. A trust must already exist to continue with your application.

Not already a trust?

Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

Visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

Content key: EntitlementEntityTypeSUP

Inline content: This means all superannuation entities including Self-Managed Super Funds (SMSFs). For a super fund to exist it must hold assets and have a trust with an appointed trustee.

Help content:

Superannuation

This means all superannuation entities including:

  • Self-Managed Super Fund (SMSF) - regulated by ATO
  • Superannuation fund - regulated by APRA
  • Non-regulated superannuation fund
  • Pooled superannuation trust
  • Approved deposit fund.
Important: This ABN application does not set up a superannuation fund! The super fund must already have a trust with an appointed trustee.

Not already a superannuation fund?

It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

Visit the Australian Tax Office (ATO) website for details on specific superannuation entity structures.

Once you?re ready to go, come back to our website to register an ABN.
