    Content key: CompanyAssociatesABNCompany

    Help content:

    Business associates

    In this section, please provide the details of all business associates of the company, including:

    • directors
    • shareholders or members
    • secretaries
    • the public officer.

    Companies must have written consent from all directors, secretaries and shareholders/members to take on their role. You don't need to provide copies, but you must keep them as part of the company's records after the company is registered.

    As the applicant, you'll be asked to declare that you have received these before you can submit this application.

    Remember! Shareholders/members can be individuals or companies, but directors and secretaries must be individuals.

    What personal information will be available to the public?

    The following information will be available to the public in the company register:

    • All directors and secretaries ? their full name, date of birth and residential address.
    • Top 20 shareholders or members (based on shareholdings) of each share class ? their name and address.

    Officeholders (directors and secretaries) can apply for approval to provide a different address in some circumstances. Visit the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) website for information about the application fee and how to apply for suppression of residential address.

    Read the summary of ASIC's privacy policy to find out how ASIC handles personal information.

    Can I get a refund?

    Can I appeal?

    Where do I display my business name?

    You're no longer required to display your record of registration. However, unless you have an exemption you must display your business name:

    • at each location where you're trading to the public (such as a shop or stall at an exhibition)
    • on all official documents (such as a quotes, tax invoices or receipts).

    See more details on where you should display your business name on the ASIC website.

    Which business details will be public?

    The Business registration service does not currently process business name updates or renewals. You can update or renew your business name on the ASIC website.

    Content key: DashboardABNPending

    Inline content:

    Thank you. This ABN application was received by the Australian Business Register (ABR), however they'll need to review the application manually. The possible reason for this could be:

    • your identity needs to be checked manually, or
    • more information is needed to finalise your application.
    Important: Please do not re-apply for an ABN while this application is being reviewed.

    Details on what happens when an application is under manual review can be found on the ABR website.

    How long will it take?

    Please allow up to 20 business days for the ABR to process your application. If you haven't heard anything from the ABR, please contact them on 13 92 26 and quote the ATO Application reference number below:

    ATO Application reference number: @Model.Reference

    What happens to my other applications?

    If you've also applied for other tax applications, they'll remain in a pending state until the manual review is finalised.

    Did you also apply for an AUSkey? If an ABN application is under manual review, a related AUSkey application is automatically unsuccessful.

    In this case you'll need to wait for an ABN number before you can register for an AUSkey again on the ABR website.

    Unfortunately this application for Goods & Services Tax (GST) was unsuccessful.

    Is GST affected by other applications?

    Yes. An Australian Business Number (ABN) is required before GST can be approved. So if your ABN application was unsuccessful, then your GST application will also be unsuccessful.

    Will this affect my other applications?

    If you have other applications that depend on the success of your GST application, then yes. If a GST application is unsuccessful then any application for fuel tax credits, luxury car tax or wine equalisation tax will also be unsuccessful.

    How do I find out more?

    To find out more about why this GST application was unsuccessful contact the ATO on 13 72 26. You'll need to quote your ATO Application reference number below:

    ATO Application reference number: @Model.Reference

    Can I appeal?

    If you've contacted the ATO and still want to appeal the decision, you can make a formal objection within 60 days. Details on how to do this can be found on the Object to an ATO decision page on the ATO website.

    Content key: Taxation

    Help content:

    GST turnover

    GST turnover is your current or projected annual turnover (excluding GST amounts) ? whichever is greater. GST turnover is not your profit.

    Current annual turnover is:

    • the value of all sales you made or are likely to make in the current month plus
    • the value of all sales you made in the previous 11 months.

    Projected annual turnover is:

    • the value of all sales you made or are likely to make in the current month plus
    • the value of all sales you're likely to make in the next 11 months.

    If you need more help working out your annual GST turnover visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website.

    Content key: CooperativeCompanyNameHelp

    Inline content: Enter the co-operative's company name exactly as it appears on the registration certificate.

    Help content:

    Co-operative company name

    Please enter the name of the co-operative exactly as it appears on the registration certificate issued by the regulatory body.

    Having trouble? The name must:

    • include the terms 'co-operative' or 'co-op', and 'limited' or 'ltd' at the end.
    • not include invalid characters (e.g. ~'!@#$%^&*_+[]{}\:;?/<>=,.).
    • not include three or more of the same letter in a row.
    • not include two or more hyphens (-), apostrophes (?), spaces ( ) or punctuation marks in a row.
    • not include terms like:
      • receivership, bankrupt, or liquidation
      • not applicable, or N/A
      • no business name, or don't have one
      • as above
      • P/I/P
      • T/A
      • does not trade
      • incorrectly registered
      • ATF, as trustee for, T'tee, Ttee, Trustee or T/tee
      • TFN
      • self-employed, self-trade, self-trading or sole trader
      • the body corporate
      • APFP.

    Content key: DashboardSearchHelp

    Help content:

    Search help

    Simple search

    The simple search only contains a Search for field. You can enter either an application reference (found at the top left of each Application summary box), Australian Business Number (ABN), Australian Company Number (ACN), company name or business name in this field and select the Find applications button to search.

    Tip: You don?t need to enter the details in full. The search will accept partial names.

    Please enter the data in the following format:

    • Application reference: e.g. 1234-AB-5678-C (use dashes '-' and remove the hash '#')
    • ABN: e.g. 12345678910 (spaces are not accepted)
    • ACN: e.g. 345678910 (spaces are not accepted)
    • Business name: e.g. Jo's Super Plumbing (partial names are accepted)
    • Company name: e.g. Jo's Plumbing Pty Ltd (partial names are accepted).

    Advanced search

    If you have 3 or more applications, the Advanced search will appear. Simply select the link Show advanced options to display the advanced search options.

    In addition to the fields available in the simple search above, the advanced search also allows you to search by submitted date and status of the application, as well as registration types. To narrow down your search, enter one or more of these filters and click the Find applications button.

    See the details for each of the advanced search options below:

    • Submitted date from: Enter a date in the format 01/01/2017 (including forward slashes '/') or select the calendar icon to pick a date.
    • Submitted date to: Enter a date in the format 31/12/2017 (including forward slashes '/') or select the calendar icon to pick a date.
    • Status of application: Use the arrow icon in the right-hand side of the box to select the Not submitted, Payment in Progress, Payment Declined, Submitted or Completed status. If you aren't sure, leave the Show all option.
    • Registration types: Select one or more types from Business name, Company, ABN, GST, PAYG, FBT, LCT, FTC, WET, and AUSKey.

    How do I return to the simple search?

    Select the Hide advanced options link.

    How do I return to my full list of applications?

    Remove all the information entered in search fields and select Find applications.

    How do I browse my applications?

    If you're browsing multiple search results, scroll to the bottom of the screen and select the Show more button to reveal more results.

    If the Show more button doesn't appear, you've reached the end of your results.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeCMT

    Inline content: Used to combine the small investments of individuals to help them access larger investment markets.

    Help content:

    Cash management trust

    A cash management trust is a type of trust set up to combine the small investments of individuals to help them access larger investment markets.

    These markets would normally only be available to professional investors with a lot more money at their disposal.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A cash management trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeDIT

    Inline content: Where a trustee chooses how to distribute income from investment activities.

    Help content:

    Discretionary investment trust

    A discretionary investment trust is a type of trust set up to help manage income from investment activities. This includes trusts set up for charitable purposes.

    Discretionary trusts are the most common trust type used for family trusts.

    In this type of trust, the income and capital amounts given to beneficiaries is not prearranged. Usually the trustee distributes these amounts at their discretion within share class types and any specified terms in the trust deed.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A discretionary investment trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeDTT

    Inline content: Where a trustee chooses how to distribute income from trading activities.

    Help content:

    Discretionary trading trust

    A discretionary trading trust is a type of trust set up to help manage the income from trading activities.

    In this type of trust, the income and capital amounts given to beneficiaries is not prearranged. Usually the trustee distributes these amounts at their discretion within share class types and any specified terms in the trust deed.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A discretionary trading trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeFXT

    Inline content: Used to automatically distribute a prearranged amount (e.g. percentage) of income or capital to each beneficiary.

    Help content:

    Fixed trust

    A fixed trust is a type of trust set up to automatically distribute prearranged or "fixed" amounts of income or capital to beneficiaries.

    Amounts are worked out according to a fraction or percentage of the trust that each beneficiary holds.

    For example: A trust has three beneficiaries. One beneficiary has a fixed entitlement to 50% or one half (½) of the trust income or capital. The remaining two beneficiaries each have a fixed entitlement to 25% or one quarter (¼) of the income or capital.

    Amounts are clearly outlined in a trust agreement and agreed on in advance.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A fixed trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeFUT

    Inline content: Used to automatically distribute a prearranged amount or unit of income or capital to each beneficiary.

    Help content:

    Fixed unit trust

    A fixed unit trust is a type of trust set up to automatically distribute prearranged or "fixed" amounts of income or capital to beneficiaries.

    Amounts are worked out according to the amount of trust units each beneficiary holds.

    For example: A trust has 100 units. One beneficiary has a fixed entitlement to 40 units. The remaining three beneficiaries have a fixed entitlement to 20 units each. These units are then used to work out what proportion of income or capital the beneficiary is entitled to.

    Amounts are clearly outlined in a trust agreement and agreed on in advance.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A fixed unit trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeHYT

    Inline content: Where a trustee distributes a prearranged amount of income or capital to beneficiaries, at their discretion.

    Help content:

    Hybrid trust

    A hybrid trust is a mixed type of trust where a trustee distributes income or capital amounts:

    • at their discretion, and
    • according to prearranged amounts that are agreed on and clearly outlined in a trust agreement.
    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A hybrid trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypePUT

    Inline content: Used to offer shares of the trust by listing on the stock exchange.

    Help content:

    Listed public unit trust

    A listed public unit trust is a type of trust that distributes prearranged amounts or shares of income and capital. The units or shares for this type of trust are offered by listing on the stock exchange.

    The amounts the beneficiaries or shareholders receive from the trust are based on the number of units or shares they hold.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! A listed public unit trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypePQT

    Inline content: Used to offer shares of the trust to the general public.

    Help content:

    Unlisted public unit trust

    An unlisted public unit trust is a type of trust that distributes prearranged amounts or shares of income and capital. The units or shares for this type of trust are offered to the general public but are not listed on the stock exchange.

    The amounts the beneficiaries or shareholders receive from the trust are based on the number of units or shares they hold.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up a trust! An unlisted public unit trust must already exist to continue with your application.

    Not already a trust?

    Trusts are complex to set up and you?ll need time and the right skills to do it properly.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you?re thinking about starting a trust.

    Once you?re ready, come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: TrustNameHelp

    Inline content: Enter the trust's legal name exactly as it appears on all official and legal documents.

    Help content:

    Trust legal name

    The trust legal name is the name that appears on all official documents and legal papers (e.g. the trust deed).

    The system will accept:

    • the terms 'Trust', 'Family Trust' or 'The trustee for'.
    • spaces
    • letters A to Z
    • numbers 0 to 9
    • standard punctuation marks such as . , ? ! ( ) { } : ; ' ? ?
    • the symbols | - _ \ / @ # $ % * = & [ ] `

    The trust name must not include:

    • three or more of the same letter in a row.
    • three or more hyphens (-), apostrophes (?), spaces ( ) or punctuation marks in a row.
    • terms like:
      • receivership, bankrupt, or liquidation
      • not applicable, NA, N''A, A/A, N/A, N A, N / A or N'A
      • don't have one
      • as above
      • P/I/P
      • T/A
      • does not trade
      • incorrectly registered
      • TFN
      • self-employed, self-trade, self-trading or sole trader
      • the body corporate
      • APFP.

    Inline content:

    Are you registered for Simplified Goods & Services Tax (GST)?

    Please note: If you register for an ABN, you will lose this GST status and will be moved to standard GST registration.

    Help content:

    GST for non-residents

    Non-residents registering for GST can elect to register under the Simplified GST system. An Australian Business Number (ABN) is not required for this type of registration.

    If a non-resident who is already registered under the Simplified GST system registers for an ABN, they will be automatically switched to standard GST registration.

    To find out more about GST registration options for non-residents, visit the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website.

    Content key: CompanyDetailsPersonAssociateABNOnlyOfficeDirector

    Help content:

    Directors

    Directors are expected to:

    • guide and monitor the management of the company
    • always act in the company's best interests
    • ensure the company complies with its legal requirements.

    To be a director, a person must:

    • have agreed in writing to be a company director
    • be at least 18 years of age.

    A director's appointment is effective on the day the company is successfully registered.

    For more about the duties of a company director, go to the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) website:

    • Your company and the law
    • Company officeholder duties

    What personal information will be available to the public?

    The name, date of birth and residential address of directors will be available to the public from the company register for a small fee.

    Read the summary of ASIC's privacy policy to find out how ASIC handles personal information.

    Who can't be a director?

    Unless a court allows it, a person must not be a director if they:

    • are bankrupt
    • are in debt and have an agreement with creditors to manage the debt
    • have been convicted of offences such as fraud or offences under the Corporations Act 2001
    • have been disqualified from managing companies.

    Find out more about bankruptcy and personal insolvency agreements while you're a director on the ASIC website.

    Content key: CompanyDetailsPersonAssociateABNOnlyOfficeSecretary

    Help content:

    Secretaries

    The day-to-day responsibilities of company secretaries may include:

    • letting ASIC know about changes to company details (such as changes to the registered office address, secretaries or directors)
    • lodging the company's financial reports
    • ensuring the company meets its legal requirements.

    To be a secretary, a person must:

    • have agreed in writing to be a company secretary
    • be at least 18 years of age.

    A secretary's appointment is effective on the day the company is successfully registered.

    Find out more about the duties of officeholders (directors and secretaries) on the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC) website.

    What personal information will be available to the public?

    The name, date of birth and residential address of company secretaries will be available to the public from the company register for a small fee.

    Read the summary of ASIC's privacy policy to find out how ASIC handles personal information.

    Who can't be a secretary?

    Unless a court allows it, a person must not be a secretary if they:

    • are bankrupt
    • are in debt and have an agreement with creditors to manage the debt
    • have been convicted of offences such as fraud or offences under the Corporations Act 2001.

    Content key: CompanyDetailsPersonAssociateABNOnlyOfficeShareholder

    Help content:

    Shareholders

    Shareholders are also known as members. Together, they own the company by owning shares in the company.

    Remember, however, that the company is a separate legal entity, so the company's assets belong to the company, not the shareholders.

    Shareholders can be individuals or companies. Company law doesn't set out a minimum age requirement for shareholders, but a company can make rules about this if they like.

    Find out more about the role of company members (shareholders) on the ASIC website.

    What information will be available to the public?

    The name and residential address of company members (shareholders) will be available to the public from the company register for a small fee.

    Read the summary of ASIC's privacy policy to find out how ASIC handles personal information.

    Content key: BusinessRegistrationsDescription

    Inline content: Welcome to the Australian Government Business Registration Service.
    Here you can apply for your key business and tax registrations in one place.

    Help content:

    Business Registration Service

    The Australian Government Business Registration Public Beta service combines a number of key government business and tax registration forms in one place.

    We have forms for new businesses, existing businesses returning to apply for tax registrations or businesses who simply need an Administrator AUSkey login. See below for more details:

    • New business

      Use the New business form if you need a new Australian Business Number (ABN). You can apply here for your ABN together with any of the following registrations:

      • Business name*
      • Goods and Services Tax (GST)
      • Australian company
      • Pay as You Go (PAYG) withholding
      • Fringe Benefits Tax (FBT)
      • Luxury Car Tax (LCT)
      • Fuel Tax Credits (FTC)
      • Wine Equalisation Tax (WET)
      • Administrator AUSkey.

      *You can also apply for business name on its own if you:

      • already have an ABN
      • already have an ABN reference number
      • operate only on Christmas or Cocos Island
      • apply as a joint venture.

    • Apply for tax registrations

      Use the Apply for tax registrations form if you already have an ABN, but need to apply for one or more tax registration.

      You can use your AUSkey or MyGov login (attached to your ABN) to apply for GST, PAYG withholding, FBT, LCT, FTC and WET.

    • Apply for AUSkey login

      Use the Apply for AUSkey login form if you already have an ABN and you either:

      • need an administrator AUSkey for yourself, or
      • already have an administrator AUSkey, but want to apply for additional AUSkeys for your business associates.

    What is a Public Beta website?

    A public beta website is typically a real working website or service in its final testing stage. A beta is used to receive public feedback to help improve the service.

    Please note: Even though the Business Registration Service is in beta, the registrations you apply for are real!

    So if you use the Business Registration Service, please give us your feedback.

    Can I register Norfolk Island businesses here?

    Yes. Norfolk Island businesses can use the New business form to apply for the following business registrations:

    • ABN
    • Business name
    • Australian company ? if operating on the Australian mainland
    • PAYG withholding
    • FBT
    • AUSKey

    Norfolk Island businesses do not need to register for GST, LCT, FTC or WET.

    Norfolk Island companies are registered with the Norfolk Island Registry.

    However, if your Norfolk Island company is or will be operating on the Australian mainland, you'll need to register as a foreign company with the Australian Securities & Investments Commission (ASIC).

    Find out about registering foreign companies on the ASIC website.

    Can I update my details or apply for renewals here?

    Not at the moment. To update or renew your registrations you'll need to refer to the correspondence you receive confirming your registration.

    If you can't find your correspondence, visit the following agency websites to:

    • update your company details or annual statements on the ASIC website
    • update or renew your business name on the ASIC website
    • update your tax details for your ABN, GST, PAYG, TFN, FBT, LCT, FTC, WET registrations on the ATO website.

    Can I apply here for state licences or permits?

    No. You'll still need to find and apply for your business licences and permits on the Australian Business Licence & Information Service (ABLIS) website.

    Where do I go for help?

    If you have a question about the form or how your registrations are progressing, contact business.gov.au on 13 28 46

    Help content:

    Business logins - AUSkey

    Only Administrator AUSkey registration is available here.

    What is an AUSkey?

    An AUSkey is a secure login that's set up on your computer. If you're eligible, AUSkey lets you log in to many government services including business and tax forms.

    What can I do with an AUSkey?

    With a compatible system or browser, an AUSkey can help you:

    • update your business name details through ASIC connect
    • lodge your Business Activity Statements (BAS) through the Business Portal
    • update your Australian Business Number (ABN) details
    • submit tax statements through 'SBR-enabled' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll desktop software.

    See where you can use your AUSkey on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    If you want to log in from different computers, you can set up an AUSkey on a USB stick.

    How do I register?

    You can only register for an Administrator AUSkey here. All you need to provide is your:

    • Australian Business Number (ABN)
    • Tax file number
    • Australian telephone number
    • Email address.

    Find out more about registering for an AUSkey on the ABR website.

    To register a tax agent or accountant for a Standard AUSkey, you'll need to register on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    You can now choose how you want to log in to manage your government business and tax details. Only AUSkey is available to register here on this Business registration form. To find out more about additional business login options, expand the "Additional logins" tab below.

    Additional logins

    You can now choose how you want to log in to manage your government business and tax details.

    You can use your AUSkey or one of the login options below:

    • Manage ABN connections
      If you have a myGov login, you can link your ABNs to your myGov account. This means you can then use your myGov account to manage your ABN details.
    • Online or 'cloud' tax software
      You can now use eligible online or 'cloud' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll software to process certain government tax forms.

    Please note: the login options above are for specific tax paperwork. You'll still need to use either your AUSkey or ASIC connect login to:

    • manage business name details or renewals
    • submit tax forms through 'SBR-enabled' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll desktop software.

    Visit the myGov website to find out more about the Manage ABN Connections option.

    Find out more about the online or 'cloud' software service on the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website.

    Content key: AuskeyRegistrationsIntro

    Inline content: Welcome to the Business Registration Service.

    An administrator AUSkey gives you full access to manage the registrations attached to an ABN and also allows you to issue additional AUSkeys to business associates.

    Help content:

    Administrator AUSkey

    Only Administrator AUSkey registration is available here.

    What is an Administrator AUSkey?

    An Administrator AUSkey gives you full access to manage the registrations attached to an ABN and also allows you to issue additional AUSkeys to business associates. An Administrator AUSkey is usually for the director or owner of a business or company.

    Important: An Administrator AUSkey is not for your accountant or tax agent. You can register them for a Standard AUSkey on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    New AUSkey

    Select the New AUSkey button if you don't already have an Administrator AUSkey. To register, you need to provide your:

    • Australian Business Number (ABN)
    • Name and role in the organisation
    • Tax File Number (TFN)
    • Date of birth
    • Australian telephone number
    • Email address.

    Additional AUSkeys

    Select the Additional AUSkeys button if you already have an Administrator AUSkey and you want additional AUSkeys to give to your business associates (who are already listed on your ABN registration).

    To register, you need to login with your AUSkey or MyGov account and provide the following details for each business associate:

    • Tax File Number (TFN)
    • Date of birth
    • Australian telephone number
    • Email address.

    Be careful who you give this AUSkey to! An administrator AUSkey gives them full access to manage the registrations attached to your ABN and also allows them to issue additional AUSkeys to others.

    To protect your security, it is also recommended you limit the number of Administrator AUSkeys you create.

    Don't have a login?

    To apply for additional AUSkey registrations, you'll need one of the following government logins:

    • Administrator AUSkey: You can apply with us for your first Administrator AUSkey.
    • MyGov: Connect your ABN to an existing MyGov account on the MyGov website.

    Find out more about registering for an AUSkey on the ABR website.

    Content key: AuskeyRegistrationsNote

    Content key: AuskeyRegistrationsNoteSingle

    Select New AUSkey below if you already have an ABN, but don?t have an Administrator AUSkey.

    Content key: AuskeyRegistrationsNoteAdditional

    Have an AUSkey?

    Select Additional AUSkeys below if you already have an Administrator AUSkey but need one or more additional Administrator AUSkeys e.g. for multiple business owners.

    Tip: Try limiting the number of Administrator AUSkeys you create to protect your security.

      @foreach(var error in Model.Errors) {

    You can expect a letter of confirmation in the mail from the Australian Business Register (ABR) within 14 days.

    You can take a copy of your ABN number by clicking the Copy button beside your ABN above.

    Which ABN details will be public?

    Only certain information will become publicly available on the ABN Lookup website.

    For a full list of ABN details displayed on the website or if you wish to suppress certain details, go to the your business information on the ABR web page.

    Where do I display my ABN?

    You must display your ABN on payment slips, receipts and tax invoices. You may also wish to display your ABN on your website, letterheads or other marketing material. Find details on these requirements below:

    • See details and examples of tax invoices on the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website.
    • Check out the information required on payslips on the Fair Work Ombudsman website.
    • Find a list of information required on receipts on the Australian Competition & Consumer Commission website.

    What else do I need to register?

    There are a number of registrations you may still need before you can start trading. State and territories have various licences and permits that are often required prior to starting your business or company.

    See the Australian Business Licence and Information Service (ABLIS) to find the licences and permits you need to run your business.

    Where do I update my details?

    The Business registration service does not currently process ABN updates. Find out how you can update your ABN details on the ATO website.

    Who can I contact?

    To find out more about your ABN registration, please contact the ABR on 13 92 26.

    Authorised contact

    If you'd like someone other than any previous authorised contacts to be contacted about this application, please add their details below.

    An authorised contact nominated here can ask the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) to change your details on your behalf. Find out more about ATO authorised contacts on the ATO website.

    Pay As You Go (PAYG) Withholding registration

    You must be registered for PAYG withholding before you need to withhold tax amounts from payments such as:

    • the wage or salary payments you make to employees
    • payments to directors
    • payments to businesses that do not quote their ABN to you
    • royalty, dividend or interest payments to non-residents
    • investment income payments to Australian residents (if you're an investment body).

    Find out more

    See how PAYG withholding works on the ATO website.

    Content key: TaxationGstDetailsIsNonForProfitOrganisation

    Help content:

    Not for profit

    A company is not for profit if it:

    • uses any profit it makes to achieve its aims
    • doesn't pay dividends to its members
    • doesn't distribute its assets to members if it is wound up.

    Not making any profit doesn't mean your company is a not-for-profit organisation.

    Examples of not-for-profit organisations include:

    • religious institutions
    • cultural societies
    • professional associations
    • social clubs.

    To find out more, go to the What type of not for profit is your organisation? page on the Australian Taxation Office website.

    Content key: ApplyForTaxesHelp

    Help content:

    Apply for additional tax registrations

    Welcome to the Australian Government Business Registration Service Public Beta. Existing businesses and companies can apply here for one or more tax registrations at the same time.

    Please note: Additional tax registrations are only available if you already have an ABN.

    What taxes can I register for?

    You can apply for one or more of the following tax roles or registrations:

    • Goods and Services Tax (GST)
    • Pay As You Go (PAYG) withholding
    • Fringe Benefits Tax (FBT)
    • Luxury Car Tax (LCT)
    • Fuel Tax Credits (FTC)
    • Wine Equalisation Tax (WET).

    Why do I need an AUSkey or MyGov login?

    An Administrator AUSkey or MyGov login (linked to an existing ABN) is required so we can access your existing ABN details.

    This is the same process you would use if you logged in to the Australian Taxation Office systems to manage your ABN details or to add tax registrations or roles.

    Don't have a login?

    To apply for one or more tax registration, you'll need one of the following government logins:

    • Administrator AUSkey: You can apply with us for your Administrator AUSkey.
    • MyGov: Connect your ABN to an existing MyGov account on the MyGov website.

    AUSkey

    Only Administrator AUSkey registration is available here.

    What is an AUSkey?

    An AUSkey is a secure login that's set up on your computer. If you're eligible, AUSkey lets you log in to many government services including business and tax forms.

    What can I do with an AUSkey?

    With a compatible system or browser, an AUSkey can help you:

    • update your business name details through ASIC connect
    • lodge your Business Activity Statements (BAS) through the Business Portal
    • update your Australian Business Number (ABN) details
    • submit tax statements through 'SBR-enabled' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll desktop software.

    See where you can use your AUSkey on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    If you want to log in from different computers, you can set up an AUSkey on a USB stick.

    What do I need to register?

    To register for a new Administrator AUSkey, you need to provide your:

    • Australian Business Number (ABN)
    • Name and role in the organisation
    • Tax File Number (TFN)
    • Date of birth
    • Australian telephone number
    • Email address.

    Find out more about registering for an AUSkey on the ABR website.

    To register a tax agent or accountant for a Standard AUSkey, you'll need to register on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    You can now choose how you want to log in to manage your government business and tax details. Only AUSkey is available to register here on this Business registration form. To find out more about additional business login options, expand the "Additional logins" tab below.

    Additional logins

    You can now choose how you want to log in to manage your government business and tax details.

    You can use your AUSkey or one of the login options below:

    • Manage ABN connections
      If you have a myGov login, you can link your ABNs to your myGov account. This means you can then use your myGov account to manage your ABN details.
    • Online or 'cloud' tax software
      You can now use eligible online or 'cloud' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll software to process certain government tax forms.

    Please note: the login options above are for specific tax paperwork. You'll still need to use either your AUSkey or ASIC connect login to:

    • manage business name details or renewals
    • submit tax forms through 'SBR-enabled' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll desktop software.

    Visit the myGov website to find out more about the Manage ABN Connections option.

    Find out more about the online or 'cloud' software service on the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) website.

    Help content:

    Administrator AUSkey

    Only Administrator AUSkey registration is available here.

    What is an Administrator AUSkey?

    An Administrator AUSkey gives you full access to manage the registrations attached to an ABN and also allows you to issue additional AUSkeys to business associates. An Administrator AUSkey is usually for the director or owner of a business or company.

    Important: An Administrator AUSkey is not for your accountant or tax agent. You can register them for a Standard AUSkey on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    Additional AUSkeys

    If you already have an Administrator AUSkey and you want additional AUSkeys to give to your business associates (who are already listed on your ABN registration) you can register here.

    To register, you need to provide the following details for each business associate:

    • Tax File Number (TFN)
    • Date of birth
    • Australian telephone number
    • Email address.

    Be careful who you give this AUSkey to! An administrator AUSkey gives them full access to manage the registrations attached to your ABN and also allows them to issue additional AUSkeys to others.

    To protect your security, it is also recommended you limit the number of Administrator AUSkey's you create.

    Find out more about registering for an AUSkey on the ABR website.

    Content key: EntitlementQuestion160

    Help content:

    Assets

    A Self-Managed Super Fund (SMSF) must set aside assets for the purpose of providing benefits to its members.

    An asset is anything tangible (e.g. property) or intangible (e.g. a patent) that is capable of being owned or controlled to produce value, and that is held to have positive economic value.

    Important: To be eligible for an ABN, a SMSF must have an amount (e.g. $10) held with the trust.

    Need more help?

    For further information on registering a SMSF, visit the ATO website.

    Content key: EntitlementAnswer400

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeSMF

    Inline content: A small private super fund that is managed by it's members. These funds are regulated by the Australian Taxation Office (ATO).

    Help content:

    ATO Regulated Self-Managed Superannuation Fund

    A self-managed superannuation fund (SMSF) is a private super fund, regulated by the Australian Taxation Office (ATO), that you manage yourself.

    An SMSF allows you to invest in shares, term deposits, managed funds and property as well as collectables such as antiques and artwork.

    Self-managed funds can have between one and four members and can be structured as:

    • a corporate trustee ? a company that acts as the trustee and each member is a director, or
    • an individual trustee ? where each members is appointed as a trustee, with a minimum of two trustees.

    Trustees are responsible for decisions made about the fund and for complying with super and tax laws.

    Important!

    Applying for an ABN doesn't automatically set up an SMSF. The super fund must already have:

    • at least one appointed trustee
    • a trust deed
    • identifiable members
    • assets put aside for the benefit of its members.

    Setting up an SMSF is complex. You'll need the assistance of a qualified, licensed professional.

    Visit the Australian Taxation Office website for information if you're thinking about starting a SMSF.

    Once you're ready, you have 60 days to come back to our website to apply for an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeARF

    Inline content: A fund regulated by the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA). The fund can be a large public fund, large private fund or a small private fund.

    Help content:

    APRA Regulated Superannuation Fund

    The Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA) supervises regulated superannuation funds that are not self-managed superannuation funds (these are regulated by the Australian Taxation Office).

    Applying for an ABN doesn't automatically set up an APRA-regulated fund. The super fund must already have a trust with an appointed trustee.

    APRA-regulated funds include:

    • Public offer funds: A fund selling superannuation services to the general public.
    • Non-public offer funds: A fund set up by one or more employers offering superannuation only to their employees.
    • Small APRA funds: A small APRA fund managed by a trustee with up to four members.
    Please note: Government entities are entitled to an ABN but cannot apply using this service. If you would like to apply for an ABN as a Government entity visit the Australian Business Register.

    Not already an APRA-regulated super fund?

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    To find out more about licensing, registration and legal obligations of APRA super funds visit the APRA website.

    Once you?re ready to go, come back to our website to register an ABN.

    Content key: EntitlementEntitySubTypeNRF

    Inline content: A certain entity type that has not elected to be a regulated fund, such as a registered financial institutions or charitable funds.

    Help content:

    Non-Regulated Superannuation Fund

    A non-regulated superannuation fund has not elected to be regulated by the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA) or the Australian Taxation Office (ATO) and is not intending to make such an election using this application. These super funds fall under government supervision instead.

    In order to be a non-regulated super fund, the fund needs to be exempt under the Superannuation Industry (Supervision) Act 1993. Examples of non-regulated super funds include:

    • registered financial institutions
    • religious charitable development funds
    • public sector superannuation scheme.
    Please note: Government entities are entitled to an ABN but cannot apply with us. If you would like to apply for an ABN as a public sector super scheme visit the Australian Business Register.

    Not already a non-regulated super fund?

    This ABN application does not set up a non-regulated superannuation fund! It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved.

    To find out more about the types of funds that can be non-regulated visit the APRA website.

    Once you?re ready to go, come back to our website to register an ABN.

    A Pooled Superannuation Trust (PST) is a type of unit trust regulated by the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA).

    Approved Deposit Fund

    An approved deposit fund (ADF) is an indefinitely continuing fund regulated by the Australian Prudential Regulation Authority (APRA).

    ADF's are maintained for the purpose of receiving, holding and investing certain types of rollover funds (e.g. termination payments) until the funds are withdrawn.

    ADFs can be either single-members or multi-members.

    Important: This ABN application does not set up an approved deposit fund! The super fund must already have a trust with an appointed trustee.

    Content key: BusinessActivitySuperannuationFundEntityStructure

    Help content:

    Structure of the entity

    Accumulation benefit fund

    Most Australians have their super in an accumulation fund. They are called accumulated funds because the benefits grow or accumulate over time.

    This type of fund calculates a benefit to the member based on the total amount of contributions received for the member plus earnings, less expenses and tax.

    Defined benefit funds

    Most defined benefit funds are corporate or public sector funds that are closed to new members.

    There are different types of defined benefit funds:

    • Defined benefit fund - all members defined benefits

      This means that all members of fund belong to a defined benefit fund.

    • Defined benefit fund - not all members defined benefits

      The fund has at least one defined benefit member, and some or all of the contributions paid into the fund are accumulated on an aggregated basis (they are not made in respect of an individual member).

    • Unfunded defined benefit fund

      In an unfunded defined benefit fund, member benefits are not financed until just before they become payable. The benefits are generally paid by an employer.

      These funds mostly cover government employees ? for example the Commonwealth Superannuation Scheme (CSS) and Public Superannuation Scheme (PSS).

    Not sure?

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you set up.

    To find out more about licensing, registration and legal obligations of super funds visit the APRA website.

    Content key: SuperannuationAPRARegulatedTypeOfFund

    Help content:

    Type of APRA fund

    Select the type of APRA superannuation fund that requires an ABN. See below for details of each type of fund.

    Non-public offer fund

    Non-public offer funds have more than four members and a membership limited to the employees of an employer or group of employers.

    Public offer fund

    This type of superannuation fund can be joined by members of the public. It is a regulated fund, consisting of pooled superannuation sold commercially, for example, through life companies, bank subsidiaries or financial planners.

    A public offer fund includes personal superannuation products and master trusts (where a large number of unconnected individuals or companies operate their superannuation arrangements under a single common trust deed).

    Small APRA fund

    Small APRA funds (SAFs) are regulated by APRA and have four or less memebers. They have a licensed trustee with an extended public licence.

    Not sure?

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand the different APRA funds.

    To find out more about licensing, registration and legal obligations of APRA super funds visit the APRA website.

    Help content:

    Self-Managed Superannuation Fund (SMSF) account details

    The account details must be held by the SMSF. Providing a trustee's personal account details, instead of the SMSF's bank account details, may result in improper early access to super benefits. This is illegal.

    If a benefit is unlawfully released, the ATO may apply significant penalties to the SMSF and the recipient of the benefits.

    Content key: SuperannuationNameHelp

    Help content:

    Superannuation name

    The superannuation fund name is the name that appears in the trust deed or governing rules.

    The system will accept:

    • spaces
    • letters A to Z
    • numbers 0 to 9
    • standard punctuation marks such as . , ? ! ( ) { } : ; ' ? ?
    • symbols | - _ \ / @ # $ % * = & [ ] `.

    The superannuation name must not include:

    • four or more of the same letter in a row
    • four or more hyphens (-), apostrophes (?), spaces ( ) or punctuation marks in a row.
    • terms like: Receivership, Bankrupt, Liquidation, P/I/P, As Trustee for, T/A, ATF, T'tee, Ttee, T'ee, T/tee, TFN, Self Employed, Self Trade, Self Trading, Sole Trader or The Body Corporate For or APFP
    • not applicable, NA, N''A, A/A, N/A, N A, N / A or N'A
    • terms like: As above, No Business Name, Don't have one, Does Not Trade, Incorrectly registered, Not Applicable
    • the phase Exec, Executor, Executrix or the The Exec in the legal name
    • the phrase P/L in any upper or lower case combination.

    Content key: CompanyAssociatesABNSuper

    Content key: CompanyAssociatesQuestionForSmsfLegalRepresentative

    Help content:

    Legal personal representatives

    A legal personal representative can be:

    • the executor of the will or the administrator of the estate of a deceased person
    • the trustee of the estate of a person under a legal disability or a minor
    • a person who holds enduring power of attorney to act on behalf of another person.

    A legal personal representative can act as a trustee or director of a corporate trustee, on behalf of:

    • a deceased member, until the death benefit becomes payable
    • a member under a legal disability
    • a minor (a parent or guardian can also act as a trustee on behalf of a minor).

    A legal personal representative can't act as a trustee on behalf of a disqualified person, such as an undischarged bankrupt.

    A legal personal representative does not include a registered tax agent or an accountant unless they meet the definition above.

    Help content:

    Election date

    A superannuation fund comes into existence after the trust deed has been signed and assets are set aside for the benefit of members.

    This usually occurs on the same day that the trust deed is executed and therefore cannot be a future date.

    Corporations (Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander)

    This is an Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander organisation that is incorporated under the Corporations (Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander) Act 2006 (CATSI Act).

    Content key: CompanyStructureCrowdSourceFunding

    Help content:

    Crowd-sourced funding

    Crowd-sourced funding (CSF) is a way for companies to raise money for their business, typically from a large number of investors that invest small amounts of money.

    Each investor can invest up to $10,000 a year in a company and in exchange they?ll receive shares in the company.

    Unlisted public companies with less than $25 million in consolidated assets and annual turnover can raise up to $5 million in a year.

    Note: Crowd-sourced funding of shares is different to the donation-based crowd funding (generally used to raise money for one-off projects) and investment-based crowd funding which commonly involves investing in a managed investment scheme.

    Answer yes to this question if you have an unlisted company and have raised or intend to raise money in exchange for shares in your company.

    Want to know more?

    Visit the MoneySmart website for information on crowd-sourced funding.

    Before you start to raise funds you should speak to an accountant or law professional.

    You may need to update your details with the ATO. If you think your details are correct and aren?t sure why they can?t be verified contact the ATO on 13 28 61.

    Help content:

    Verify your identity

    The Australian Taxation Office (ATO) is responsible for processing applications for an ABN and tax registrations, such as GST and PAYG withholding.

    When you apply for these registrations, your identification will be verified with the ATO against other sources, such as your ATO tax records. This allows us to confirm who you are and helps to prevent identity theft.

    To process this application quicker, we?d like to verify your identity now.

    You can continue and submit your application without updating your details, however the ATO will still need to verify your identification. This will cause a delay in your application being processed.

    To update your details with the ATO, visit their website. If you think your details are correct and aren?t sure why they can?t be verified contact the ATO on 13 28 61.

    Content key: HelpMeDecideAUSkeyInformation

    Content key: HelpMeDecideBusinessStructureSuperannuation

    Inline content: This means all superannuation entities including Self-Managed Super Funds (SMSFs). For a super fund to exist it must hold assets and have a trust with an appointed trustee.

    Help content:

    Superannuation entities

    This means all superannuation entities including:

    • Self-Managed Super Fund (SMSF) - regulated by ATO
    • Superannuation fund - regulated by APRA
    • Non-regulated superannuation fund
    • Pooled superannuation trust
    • Approved deposit fund.

    Using a superannuation structure means that a business or businesslike activity (such as charitable, leasing or one-off transactions) is held and controlled by an individual or corporate trustee for the benefit of others (the beneficiaries).

    A trustee is responsible for everything in the trust, including income and losses, and must report income in a trust income tax return.

    Applying for an ABN does not set up a superannuation fund! The super fund must already have a trust with an appointed trustee.

    It's best to see a qualified, licensed professional to help you understand what?s involved and the registrations you'll need.

    Visit the Australian Tax Office (ATO) website for details on specific superannuation entity structures.

    Key facts for superannuation entities

    • Cost - higher cost to set up
    • Setting up process - complicated
    • Responsibility for business decisions - trustee
    • Responsibility for debts - trustee
    • Report business income - on trust income tax return
    • The money you get from the business - as a beneficiary, you report any distributions on your individual tax return (if you're the trustee and there is net trust income, you're taxed at the highest marginal tax rate)
    • Tax rate - depending on the trust deed, the trust may need to pay at the company tax rate. If all income is distributed to adult beneficiaries who are Australian residents, the trust doesn't need to pay tax
    • Business Tax file number (TFN) needed - yes
    • Additional administration - the trustee is responsible for formal deed and yearly administrative tasks
    • Additional reporting - yes, the trustee is responsible for annual company tax return and other requirements
    • Separate bank account - yes

    Content key: HelpMeDecideAUSkeyLegend

    Inline content: Would you like to use an AUSkey to manage your registrations?

    Help content:

    AUSkey

    What is an AUSkey?

    An AUSkey is a secure login that's set up on your computer. If you're eligible, AUSkey lets you log in to many government services including business and tax forms.

    What can I do with an AUSkey?

    With a compatible system or browser, an AUSkey can help you:

    • update your business name details through ASIC connect
    • lodge your Business Activity Statements (BAS) through the Business Portal
    • update your Australian Business Number (ABN) details
    • submit tax statements through 'SBR-enabled' accounting, bookkeeping or payroll desktop software.

    See where you can use your AUSkey on the Australian Business Register (ABR) website.

    If you want to log in from different computers, you can set up an AUSkey on a USB stick.

    Find out more about registering for an AUSkey on the ABR website.

    Help content:

    Verifying your business associate's identity

    The Australian Taxation Office (ATO) is responsible for processing applications for an ABN and tax registrations, such as GST and PAYG withholding.

    When you apply for these registrations, your business associate's identification will be verified with the ATO against other sources, such as their ATO tax records. This allows us to prevent identity theft.

    If your business associate's details don't match up with our records, you'll be asked check their details and correct any errors.

    You can submit your application without updating these details, however the ATO will still need to verify your business associate's identification. This will cause a delay in your application being processed.

    Read our privacy policy for details on how we collect and use your information.

    Content key: HelpMeDecideBusinessNameRegisterYesSuper

    Inline content: You need to register a business name if it's different to the name of your superannuation fund (the legal name you give your fund when you register it).

    For example, if the name of your superannuation fund is Emily Patel Super Fund and you want to use the name E.P. Dentistry as your business name, you need to register it.

    Content key: HelpMeDecideBusinessNameRegisterNoSuper

    Inline content: You don't need to register your business name if it's the same as your superannuation fund's name.

    For example, if the name of your superannuation fund is Emily Patel Super Fund and you want to use it as your business name, you don't need to register it.

    Content key: HelpMeDecideBusinessNameRegisterYesTrust

    Inline content: You need to register a business name if it's different to the name of your trust (the legal name you give your trust when you register it).

    For example, if your trust's name is The Williams Family Trust and you want to use the name Smart Constructions as your business name, you need to register it.

    Content key: HelpMeDecideBusinessNameRegisterNoTrust

    Inline content: You don't need to register your business name if it's the same as your trust's name.

    For example, if the name of your trust is Williams Constructions Trust and you want to use it as your business name, you don't need to register it.
